From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Sat Dec  1 08:23:22 2007
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Sat, 01 Dec 2007 08:23:22 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Rip CD software
In-Reply-To: <d0ad9b7e0711270723m3339ff8fpeb219ec9a3590685@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d0ad9b7e0711270723m3339ff8fpeb219ec9a3590685@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1196526202.12087.15.camel@willow.odshp.com>

On Tue, 2007-11-27 at 07:23 -0800, Paul Charles Leddy wrote:
> I've got a Japanese language course on 12 CDs I want to rip to mp3. On
> Mac, all the mp3 info is perfect, but the CD drive is very slow and
> unable to read the scratched disks, so hangs. On Linux, ripping flies,
> but the mp3 info is very incomplete.
> 
> The core issue with these language courses is you want the tracks to
> play in order on your mp3 device automatically, which I assume means
> the track info has to be stored in the mp3 info, but not completely
> sure, it might be based on the stored title.
> 
> So, anyone know of good Linux ripping software that does as good a job
> at creating mp3 info as iTunes?

What I use these days:
 o Sound Juicer, with MusicBrainz support (I used 'grip' until recently,
but I have since found SJ to be easier and has built-in MusicBrainz
support)
 o If I need CDDB support, I use the MusicBrainz gateway:
http://musicbrainz.org/doc/FreeDBGateway
 o Tag Tool (MusicBrainz has a tag editor called "Picard", but it hasn't
been in the Fedora repos until very recently, so I have not had much
chance to use it)

The few music players that I have used have sorted on track number by
default (after grouping by artist and title), which is oddly sensible
and doesn't actually require reference data sources like most of the
other attributes.

Wil



From pcleddy at gmail.com  Sat Dec  1 09:26:57 2007
From: pcleddy at gmail.com (Paul Charles Leddy)
Date: Sat, 1 Dec 2007 09:26:57 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] appBase
Message-ID: <d0ad9b7e0712010926o7d1af713sced3df6f59fcbcdb@mail.gmail.com>

One other thing we have to look at: in getting rid of appBase, the
files are no longer shared between apps. So, does this effect the
performance in any way?

I say we set up 25 instances of the app in 5 instances of tomcat and
hit it w/ jmeter. then go to 50 or more.

We may want to do away w/ undeploy -- I can't think why we would need
it -- and just use a shared appBase, if performance degrades w/o it.
But I doubt it, as long as there is sufficient disk space to hold the
cached files.

And, btw, as soon as an app is shutdown, or tomcat itself, all the
appBase files in the work directory are removed by tomcat. So, they
don't linger.

On Sat, 1 Dec 2007 02:50:55 -0800
"Daniel Johnson" <teknotus at gmail.com> dijo:

> > I recently gave up on Gutsy with my Intel 3945.  Either the firmware coming from
> > Intel is crappy, or NetworkManager has taken a step backwards; I would get
> > 30-120 minutes of use before I would have to reboot to get wifi working again.
> > I broke down and grabbed a spare Linksys PCCard running with a bcm43xx driver.
> 
> I figured out that if I "sudo killall NetworkManager" followed by
> "sudo NetworkManager" all becomes right as rain again.

At home I am wired so I use wireless only away from home, which 90% of
the time is at PSU. Next time I am there I will give this a try.

My T61 has the Intel 4965AGN wireless chip and it "disconnects" me
anywhere from a few minutes to an hour or so after connecting. That is,
everything says I am still connected, but I suddenly can't go anywhere.
I use Wifi Radar mostly, because network manager can't even seem to
scan for networks. If I open Wifi Radar after being "disconnected" it
shows me as still connected and still shows the IP address.

When I boot I can immediately launch Firefox, try to go to PSU home
page, and I will always get the login screen and be able to log in to
pbnet.pdx.edu. Thereafter it is fine until I get "disconnected."
Network manager shows no change, but then, it never tells me much. From
the command line ifconfig shows everything normal. I have to reboot to
get wireless working again, and once even that didn't work - I had to
go into the BIOS, disable radio, boot, shut down and reboot, go into
the BIOS again, enable radio, and then finally boot to get the wireless
back.

Yesterday I discovered that by alternating between command line and
Wifi Radar I could get it working again without rebooting. I used "sudo
ifconfig down -a," then launched Wifi Radar to make sure it found no
networks, then "sudo ifconfig up -a." That still did not connect me.
For example, if I tried going to PSU home with Firefox it would still
not go there. But at that point I could launch Wifi Radar again, it
would see the networks, I could use Wifi Radar to connect to
pubnet.pdx.edu and get an IP address, and then Firefox would give me
the pubnet.pdx.edu login window again. 

This is a PITA. I understand the problem is the driver that Intel wrote
for 64-bit Linux. As far as I know it affects only 64-bit and only the
4965AGN chip. I have also read a couple of similar complaints from
users of 64-bit Vista.

Next time I am somewhere and get "disconnected" I will try the killall
trick to see if that works. It would be faster and simpler than what I
have been doing. Meantime, I would like to diagnose more accurately
exactly what is happening. I know next to nothing of how networking
works, let alone wireless. But there should be some command line things
I could use, or log files I could look at, that would tell the exact
story. Knowing exactly what is happening strikes me as the first step
toward fixing the problem - assuming that I can fix it from my end
without begging Intel for a better driver.

                             MEETING ANNOUNCEMENT

                        The Portland Linux/Unix Group
                                  will meet
                          7 PM Thursday Dec 6, 2007
                                      at
                          Portland State University
                                      in
                            Smith Memorial Center
                                 Room 294
       SW Montgomery, SW Broadway (7th), SW Harrison, and SW Park (9th)

      *******************************************************************

                                 PRESENTATION

                                 Introduction
                                      to
                          The R Programming Language

                                      by

                                 Brian Knaus
                       <knausb at science.oregonstate.edu>

      R is an Open Source implementation of the S statistical
      programming language.  In fact, R is the most widely used
      open source software package for statistical software development
      and data analysis, and has become a de-facto standard among
      statisticians for the development of statistical software.

      R supports a wide variety of statistical and numerical techniques
      and has excellent graphical facilities, which can produce
      publication-quality graphs which can include such things as
      mathematical symbols and maps and other complex features.
      R is also highly extensible through the use of packages,
      which are user-submitted libraries for specific functions
      or specific areas of study.  As a result, R has been extended
      to work well with postgres, GRASS, and many other software products.

      *******************************************************************

> > but the mp3 info is very incomplete.

> support)

> been in the Fedora repos until very recently, so I have not had much
> chance to use it)
>

From mikeraz at patch.com  Tue Dec  4 06:01:53 2007
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Tue, 4 Dec 2007 06:01:53 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Rip CD software
In-Reply-To: <d0ad9b7e0712021934i4784ae8bobf9da01e51c2c97c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d0ad9b7e0711270723m3339ff8fpeb219ec9a3590685@mail.gmail.com>
	<1196526202.12087.15.camel@willow.odshp.com>
	<d0ad9b7e0712021934i4784ae8bobf9da01e51c2c97c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071204140153.GA19234@patch.com>

Paul Charles Leddy wrote:
> Ya, that's what I need, track numbering in the ID3 tags. Because each
> Barron's language CD has over 50 tracks, and they need to be played in
> order automatically, especially on an iPod like device, for correct
> flow of the course material.

My ripping is done through the K3b frontend which uses lame for mp3 encoding.
The inclusion of track numbers is directly supported. 

My lame configuration is:
lame -h --tt %t  --ta %a --tl %m --ty %y --tn %n --tc %c - %f -V 0 --add-id3v2 

Where --tn is the lame argument for track number and %n provides the value. 

The track number is derived from the physical layout of the CD.  All other
information comes from cddb lookups.

Other infobits:
%t - Title
%a - Artist
%m - Album Title
%y - Release Year
%n - Track number
%c - Comment
%r - Album Artist
%x - Album comment

--

> On Tue, 27 Nov 2007 08:11:31 -0800 (PST)

>>
>> My t42 has a control button that seems to work no
>> matter which OS I am running, which turns the wireless
>> and bluetooth on and off.  For me its Function key +
>> F5.  Might it be something like that?
>
> Indeed. I bought my T61 from a local dealer on a Saturday, and   
> waited until our local Linux user group's monthly Linux Clinic on   
> the followng Sunday to install Linux on it. I started with a fresh   
> Gutsy x86_64 DVD that I had burned previously. The first thing I did  
>  was wipe out the NTFS and FAT32 partitions and install Gutsy.   
> Everything was recognized and worked perfectly, except the wireless   
> and the bluetooth. Those two lights never came on. The local Linux   
> gurus (several of whom have T43s) scratched their heads. After about  
>  20 minutes of installing this, reinstalling that, one of them   
> noticed that the switch on the front of the machine was not on. We   
> turned it on, the bluetooth light came on, and wireless worked. Duh!
>
> Having said that, I later discovered a problem with the wireless. It  
>  works great when it works, but I get suddenly disconnected. It's as  
>  though the connection to the antenna was intermittent, or the local  
>  provider was pulling the switch. This will happen anywhere from   
> immediately after booting to an hour after being online. At first I   
> was afraid I was going to have to send the machine in for repair,   
> but then I discovered others with the same problem. One place it has  
>  been discussed is here:
>
> http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=3839319&highlight=T61+wireless#post3839319
>
> And if you search on Ubuntu forums (Advanced search) for keywords   
> "T61" and "wireless" you will get several additional threads.   
> Evidently the problem is the Intel driver, which Intel knows about   
> and is apparently trying to resolve.
>
> Regarding bluetooth, that is working flawlessly. I am now using a   
> Logitech V270 bluetooth mouse. I was completely new to bluetooth so   
> I had to google for a bit to educate myself. Ultimately I discovered  
>  Blueman (sorry, didn't bookmark the link). It is not in the Ubuntu   
> repositories, but you can download either a .deb or .rpm and install  
>  with whatever installer you prefer. It is the missing bluetooth   
> utiity that Linux has been needing. I just turned on the mouse, hit   
> the Scan button in Blueman, and it found the mouse. Then I clicked   
> on Bond, Blueman popped up a window asking for the key, I entered   
> 0000, and Blueman paired it right up. Ever since it "just works." I   
> reboot the computer and there it is.
>
> I also bought a pair of Sony DR-BT50 headphones. These are serious   
> audiophile bluetooth headphones. Again, Blueman paired them up with   
> the same ease as it did the mouse. All I have to do is turn them on   
> before launching a multimedia app and the sound comes out of the   
> headphones instead of the speakers or the headphone jack. That is,   
> every app except RealPlayer. Of course, RealPlayer is the one app I   
> really need, dammit. But that's a problem with Helix, not the   
> bluetooth driver or ALSA.
>
> And regarding Alsamixer, I know little of its settings, but there   
> are some configurations in Preferences or Settings or something   
> where you can enable more stuff. And in my efforts to get RealPlayer  
>  working with bluetooth I have scoured Synaptic searching on "sound"  
>  and similar keywords. I note there are a lot of additional   
> utilities. Perhaps you don't have all of the right ones installed.
>
> I can't offer any suggestions at all about the card reader. I have   
> no devices that use the card reader, so I have never looked at it. I  
>  don't know if mine is working or not.
>
> A friend in our local LUG also recently bought a T61 and reported   
> that he has the finger thingy working. I never bothered.
>
> There is a problem (a bug report filed some time ago) with the USB   
> ports on the right rear corner. They work fine when you first boot,   
> but if you ever remove a device from either one of them, they both   
> die. The one in the middle of the left side works perfectly,   
> however. And I bought a docking station that has four USB ports in   
> the back. They all work perfectly.
>
> There was a problem at first with the volume controls. Flashing the   
> BIOS to the latest (a couple weeks ago) fixed them. However, even   
> after flashing the BIOS, I thought they were not working. That was   
> because I did not understand how they worked. I assumed the mute   
> button (on the left) was a toggle. But it does not unmute the sound   
> if you are muted. It is only a mute button. Once you are muted you   
> unmute by pressing the volume up button. It would be nice if it had   
> occurred to Lenovo to include a little user guide with this thing.
>
> Brightness (Fn+Home and Fn+Ed) do not work at all. I don't know of   
> anyone who has gotten them working with Ubuntu. I have read that   
> they do work in Linux if you shell out to a command line first   
> (Ctrl-Alt-F1), but then you can't see what it is doing. And even   
> that didn't work for me. Luckily, I don't really care. The screen is  
>  permanently on its brightest setting, and that is where I want it.
>
> I haven't tried any of the other Fn or special buttons. I've pressed  
>  the thinkVantage key now and then, but it appears dead. But then,   
> since there is no user guide, I don't know what it's supposed to do.  
>  Except I did discover that it gets me into the BIOS during the   
> initial boot process. Once Ubuntu is up, it does nothing.
>
> I'm not very good at Linux, so I probably can't offer much in the   
> way of troubleshooting advice. But at least I can relate my   
> experience so everyone knows that it is possible to get some of this  
>  stuff working.

I have a T61 working with Gutsy without much hassle at all.
Following the Thinkwiki guide to installing and configuring,  
everything works (sound, usb, wifi, card reader).
The only problem I have is that Compiz has some hardware overlay  
issues with the Intel GMA3100 video, which will hopefully be resolved  
in a driver update.

All volume controls, mute, brightness, Media keys (next track, pause,  
etc), special functions buttons like Sleep, Monitor Mode, Lock, and  
EasyJect all work as well with zero configuration.

http://www.thinkwiki.org/wiki/Installing_Ubuntu_7.10_%28Gutsy_Gibbon%29_on_a_ThinkPad_T61

The T61, despite some minor driver issues which are mostly resolved,  
has been pleasent to use under Ubuntu

 From the Wiki though, it looks like those with Nvidia cards, and the  
N wireless adapters still have some small issues.

                             MEETING ANNOUNCEMENT

                        The Portland Linux/Unix Group
                                  will meet
                          7 PM Thursday Dec 6, 2007
                                      at
                          Portland State University
                                      in
                            Smith Memorial Center
                                 Room 294
       SW Montgomery, SW Broadway (7th), SW Harrison, and SW Park (9th)

      *******************************************************************

                                 PRESENTATION

                                 Introduction
                                      to
                          The R Programming Language

                                      by

                                 Brian Knaus
                       <knausb at science.oregonstate.edu>

      R is an Open Source implementation of the S statistical
      programming language.  In fact, R is the most widely used
      open source software package for statistical software development
      and data analysis, and has become a de-facto standard among
      statisticians for the development of statistical software.

      R supports a wide variety of statistical and numerical techniques
      and has excellent graphical facilities, which can produce
      publication-quality graphs which can include such things as
      mathematical symbols and maps and other complex features.
      R is also highly extensible through the use of packages,
      which are user-submitted libraries for specific functions
      or specific areas of study.  As a result, R has been extended
      to work well with postgres, GRASS, and many other software products.

From mikeraz at patch.com  Thu Dec  6 13:01:06 2007
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2007 13:01:06 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] ssh disconnects on gutsy gibbon - partial resolution
In-Reply-To: <20071206194705.GA734@nxnw.org>
References: <30099.170.135.241.46.1196882611.squirrel@mail.patch.com>
	<20071206194705.GA734@nxnw.org>
Message-ID: <27103.170.135.241.46.1196974866.squirrel@mail.patch.com>


Steve Beattie wrote:
> Any chance that the dhcp address is accidentally being used by another
> machine?

No.  We have ~60,000 dhcp clients.  If dup addresses were a problem it would be a
known problem.

> Is it just ssh sessions, or are other connections dropped as well?

As stated before, the only persisting sessions are ssh.

        Partial Resolution

We changed the address to a static DHCP config.
We (ahem, I'm working with windows folks) the machine after correcting the time
configuration.

I'm inclined to believe that having the clock out of sync with the clients was the
root of the problem.

I term this a partial resolution because I don't know why it's working now, just
that it is.

   Michael Rasmussen, Portland, Ore, USA

From ken at scottshill.com  Thu Dec  6 15:53:23 2007
From: ken at scottshill.com (Ken Hill)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2007 15:53:23 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wifi card
In-Reply-To: <665390.7832.qm@web50612.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <665390.7832.qm@web50612.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <001d01c83863$307c4f30$9174ed90$@com>

Linux has not caught up with the world of Wifi. The hardware drivers seem to
be a problem. I've had good luck using a Linksys PC Card (Model Noumber
WPC11 version 3). I've had good luck with the Ubuntu Linux distro to detect
this card. 

You can try using ndiswrapper, but that is just a tool/wrapper program that
allows Linux to use the Microsoft Windows driver.

Good luck!

Ken

Subject: [PLUG] Wifi card
In-Reply-To: <665390.7832.qm@web50612.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <665390.7832.qm@web50612.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <55cf303a0712070910o414de0a6hc92eed02274b638c@mail.gmail.com>

On Dec 6, 2007 3:46 PM, Robert Kopp <iconoklastic at yahoo.com> wrote:

> When I ordered a laptop, the vendor provided a random PCMCIA wireless
> adapter, Airlink 101 (AWLC3028). Knoppix does not recognize it out of the
> box. (I do not yet have Linux installed on the laptop HD.) Still, this
> indicates that the installation will probably be tricky--madwifi,
> ndiswrapper, or whatever. Is this card properly supported in Linux? Or
> should I get a different one, if my intention is to use Wifi with Linux?
>

You need the MadWifi drivers.  That card is an Atheros chipset.  I have a
similar card and it works fine with that set of drivers.

In Fedora, it is easy. You use one of the repositories that has the madwifi
package and install it.  (I use the one off FreshRPMs.net.)  It compiles the
kernel module for you.  Very easy.  Not certain what you do to get it to
work with Knoppix.


From nickaubert at gmail.com  Fri Dec  7 14:04:27 2007
From: nickaubert at gmail.com (Nick Aubert)
Date: Fri, 7 Dec 2007 14:04:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wifi card
In-Reply-To: <55cf303a0712070910o414de0a6hc92eed02274b638c@mail.gmail.com>

Message-ID: <55ef240d0712071404u3eebe3b6wf04bebac85b160cd@mail.gmail.com>

Linux support for Atheros chipsets is pretty good.  Two years ago I
had to do quite a bit of work to get the madwifi drivers working on my
laptop.  A week ago I set up a Gentoo laptop with an Atheros wifi
card, and it was a snap, even with WPA encryption via wpa_supplicant.
I don't know how Knoppix does with madwifi, but kernel support is
definitely there.

Check out this article, it might have what you're looking for:
http://www.linux.com/articles/36883?tid=65&tid=81

-Nick

From russell at personaltelco.net  Fri Dec  7 18:52:37 2007
From: russell at personaltelco.net (Russell Senior)
Date: 07 Dec 2007 18:52:37 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wifi card
In-Reply-To: <55ef240d0712071404u3eebe3b6wf04bebac85b160cd@mail.gmail.com>

Message-ID: <86k5nphp8q.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Nick" == Nick Aubert <nickaubert at gmail.com> writes:

Nick> Linux support for Atheros chipsets is pretty good.  Two years
Nick> ago I had to do quite a bit of work to get the madwifi drivers
Nick> working on my laptop.  A week ago I set up a Gentoo laptop with
Nick> an Atheros wifi card, and it was a snap, even with WPA
Nick> encryption via wpa_supplicant.  I don't know how Knoppix does
Nick> with madwifi, but kernel support is definitely there.

Madwifi has indeed been one of the more solid linux drivers.  But
considering that none of them has been *that* solid, it might fall
into the category of "faint praise".  Historically, the hostap-driver
for prism chips was really solid.  Some of the other 11b devices had
decent if divergent support.  I have been using madwifi-old for a
couple years with the atheros radio in my thinkpad (I am sticking with
madwifi-old because it works reliably and since I am often diagnosing
weirdness at PTP nodes, I would rather not have that muddled up by
having weirdness on my own radio.  I've used madwifi-ng extensively in
embedded applications, which has been less solid for me.  Madwifi
(both -old and -ng) relies on a binary blob, the so-called HAL
(hardware abstraction layer).  Over the last year to 18 months there
has been a lot of work on the "mac80211" wifi stack for linux, and in
in the last few months also the ath5k driver for atheros radios.  I
haven't tried it yet, but my impression from reading the relevant
mailing lists is that it's still a bit rough.  Which is completely
understandable, considering the lack of support that most driver
writers get from hardware vendors.  My guess is that it'll be another
6 months before things really start converging on "solid" and wifi
support gets better on linux.  In the meantime, find whatever life
raft you can.  "There's hope.  No Luke Skywalker in sight."

  <http://lkml.org/lkml/2006/1/5/671>


-- 
Russell Senior, Secretary
russell at personaltelco.net

This is actually a problem for the UNIX class I'm taking. (We're not 
supposed to collaborate with other students on this, but we ARE allowed 
to seek help on the net, etc). Here is the question and the hint 
provided by the instructor.

:QUESTION [40 pts]
      Write a bash script that reads a submission file, extracts all sed
      programs, and then runs the sed program against a COPY of the
      submission file.

HINT
      My bash script uses grep and sed, but awk also could be used.  I use
      the script to process submissions.  In order to simpify this
      question, however, I will make the following unrealistic
      assumptions:

        -All sed commands are one-liners
        -All sed commands start and end with ' and have NO embedded '
         or " characters.
        -All sed commands start at the beginning of a line, and can be
         found with:
               grep -r "^sed[^']*'" | cut -f2 -d"'"
        - The above grep will find ONLY sed commands

          These assumptions are NOT realistic as far as the "real world" but
          should make the script easier to write.  Your script can accept a
          file name on the command line, then create a backup copy.  You 
can use
          the grep command to extract all of the sed programs from the file.
          Think about using a second command file to process the grep 
output.
          To process a file line by line you can use the "read" command.  If
          "myCmd" is the script:
     
      #!/bin/bash
      while read line
      do
        echo "Line: $line"
          done
     
      then you can process a file with the sequence "cat file | myCmd"

From nickaubert at gmail.com  Tue Dec 11 13:02:01 2007
From: nickaubert at gmail.com (Nick Aubert)

	<475DC049.4070509@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <55ef240d0712111302u4de3ea9oc008cdb131114feb@mail.gmail.com>

Robert's advice is a good place to start.   If your professor hasn't
provided you with a usable sample file, make one for yourself and
start testing your script with it.  Don't try to write the final
version of the script all at once.  Start by writing something really
simple, like the "read" example your professor gave.  Once it works
like you expect, then go to the next step.  The next step could be,
say, spitting out only the lines that start with the word "sed".  Keep
iterating until your script meets the requirements.  Even if you're
not sure about the whole structure at the outset, start playing with
it and the logic will come to you.

Good luck!

-Nick

From nickaubert at gmail.com  Tue Dec 11 14:10:17 2007
From: nickaubert at gmail.com (Nick Aubert)
Date: Tue, 11 Dec 2007 14:10:17 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Syllable...
In-Reply-To: <20071210222607.c2562e39.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <20071210110611.p8krlt63sw4s4sc0@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
	<20071210222607.c2562e39.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <55ef240d0712111410j798faa39vb3abd7245d158a62@mail.gmail.com>

Syllable is in fairly early stages of development.  I think of it as
somewhat equivalent to Linux in the pre-2.0 days.  It probably isn't
the ideal choice if you just want to get things done.  On the other
hand, if you manage to get ethernet working under it, you'll probably
have learned something interesting along the way.  With an OS at this
stage of development, that's probably the best you can hope for, and
kind of the whole point.  By the way, Syllable's AFS file system is
the AtheOS File System, not Andrew File System.

>From what I've read, ReactOS is basically the same as Wine, but
without Unix underneath.  So it isn't likely to run Windows programs
any better than Wine.  I'm not saying this to discourage you from
trying it out, but you should set your expectations accordingly.  If
Wine/ReactOS ever does get to the point of drop-in replacement for
Windows, expect Microsoft to go all out with patent lawsuits on every
obvious and trivial idea they ever copied from anyone else.

-Nick

On Tue, 11 Dec 2007, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> I've been googling for the past several hours.

   Hope you didn't strain your throat. Gnucash is nice for personal finance
and tries to be applicable to businesses, too. But, there is a large
difference in the needs of each market and software that tries to bridge the
gap is usually much less efficient than those aimed at one market or the
other.

> Also, are there any small business alternatives besides GnuCash and
> QuickBooks?

   I strongly recommend SQL-Ledger <http://www.sql-ledger.com/>. While it has
more bells and whistles than many of us need, it includes everything that we
do need. It can appear overwhelming at first because it's designed for
manufacturing->distribution->retailing (including POS), but it's used by a
very broad range of product- and service-providing businesses employing 1 to
many people.

   Inventory is a central feature. I have various services and business
travel expenses as inventory items so I can use them when preparing an
invoice.

   I believe that there are filters for importing QuackBooks data; however,
since I never used any of those Intuit products I really don't know.

Rich

Though I wouldn't give as strong a recommendation, I use SQL-Ledger for
my company (16 person software dev/IT services).

Web based is nice as I can give our accountants/tax-people remote access
 and is OS agnostic for the end user.

We are soon going to be using the check printing feature.

A group of people were not happy with the way the project was being run
and forked it into LedgerSMB (http://www.ledgersmb.org/).  I have no
experience with this and looking at the website shows the latest release
dated 5 days ago.

We were originally drawn to it (3 years ago) due to it being one of the
few FOSS accounting packages out there, and it's backend was originally
based on PostgreSQL (which were big fans of).

>  and is OS agnostic for the end user.

> A group of people were not happy with the way the project was being run
> and forked it into LedgerSMB (http://www.ledgersmb.org/).  I have no
> experience with this and looking at the website shows the latest release
> dated 5 days ago.

LedgerSMB is sponsored (?) by Command Prompt Inc.  I talked to Josh 
Drake at the Postgresql Conference last month about LedgerSMB.  The 
community had, interestingly enough, the same concerns that I had years 
ago when I used SQL-Ledger.  These were mostly about the model.  I.e. 
money was stored as floats, no real referential integrity, etc.  The 
change log for LedgerSMB indicates even some logic/coding issues but I 
suspect they are in both SQL-Ledger and LedgerSMB.
    This is not to 'dis' Dieter.  At the time I used SQL-Ledger I had a 
payed support contact and even though I posted questions to the main 
mailing list I usually got replies from Dieter before the post had made 
it back to me.
    That is service.

I suggest you look at both.  Neither are trivial to install.


Rod

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Wed Dec 12 11:02:51 2007
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Wed, 12 Dec 2007 11:02:51 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM Question
In-Reply-To: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031036@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
References: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031036@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
Message-ID: <4760305B.1040804@seitzassoc.com>

Daniel.Roberts at sanofi-aventis.com wrote:
> Hello All
> 
> On a redhat system..how can I figure out when rpm was last run?
> I am trying to figure out if someone besides myself is running RPM...or
> possibly how if at all a package which I thought got installed has now
> been removed ed..

This isn't exactly what you want, but it's a start.  This command will 
show all installed packages, sorted by install time.

rpm -qa --last

According to section 6.2.1.1 of this document:
http://docs.fedoraproject.org/drafts/rpm-guide-en/ch06s02.html
the following command will show a removal ID if one exists.

rpm -qa --qf "%-20{NAME} %-20{REMOVETID}\n"

I'm not sure whether to trust this.  I'm not seeing any removed 
packages on my system, which I don't believe is correct.  In fact, it 
looks as if the database that would contain this 
info(/var/lib/rpm/Removetid) does not exist on my Centos 4.5 system.

galen


From ianburrell at gmail.com  Wed Dec 12 11:04:12 2007
From: ianburrell at gmail.com (Ian Burrell)
Date: Wed, 12 Dec 2007 11:04:12 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM Question
In-Reply-To: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031028@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
References: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031028@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
Message-ID: <d91f09cd0712121104see55aeevdae7e2107495e16c@mail.gmail.com>

On Dec 12, 2007 10:13 AM,  <Daniel.Roberts at sanofi-aventis.com> wrote:
>
> On a redhat system..how can I figure out when rpm was last run?
> I am trying to figure out if someone besides myself is running RPM...or
> possibly how if at all a package which I thought got installed has now
> been removed ed..
> Thanks for any tips!
>

You can't tell when rpm was last run.  But you can tell when the
latest package was installed. rpm has a --qf flag that allows setting
the query format.  One of tags is INSTALLTIME.  I think there is even
a way to format it as a date.

rpm -qa --qf '%{NAME} %{INSTALLTIME} %{INSTALLTIME:date}\n' | sort -n -k2

This won't tell you who did the install.  You will have to check login
or sudo logs for that.

Yum also keeps a log of package changes it made in /var/log/yum.log.

 - Ian

Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/


From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Wed Dec 12 13:08:04 2007
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Wed, 12 Dec 2007 13:08:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM Question
In-Reply-To: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031028@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
References: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031028@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
Message-ID: <1197493684.21733.13.camel@willow.odshp.com>

On Wed, 2007-12-12 at 13:13 -0500, Daniel.Roberts at sanofi-aventis.com
wrote:

> On a redhat system..how can I figure out when rpm was last run?
> I am trying to figure out if someone besides myself is running RPM...or
> possibly how if at all a package which I thought got installed has now
> been removed ed..

As Paul mentioned, if your filesystem is mounted with 'noatime' (they
aren't by default), you can examine the last access time of /bin/rpm:

$ ls -lu /bin/rpm 

If that only gives you the date (maybe it's today), you can use 'stat'
to view the contents of the inode, including the access time with
seconds. That's the last time it was _accessed_, but is most likely the
time the command was run. Of course, if you've been running it...

Depending on which version and how recent, you might also have logs
in /var/log/rpmpkgs*.

It's also possible that yum is being used, in which case you can grep
for 'yum' in /var/log/messages*

Wil 



From heinlein at madboa.com  Wed Dec 12 13:17:42 2007
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Wed, 12 Dec 2007 13:17:42 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] RPM Question
In-Reply-To: <4760305B.1040804@seitzassoc.com>
References: <D04DAF1C0FD50A4F96F51B5AF2E8922D031036@BWPW05.f2.enterprise>
	<4760305B.1040804@seitzassoc.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.0.99999.0712121205430.4550@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Wed, 12 Dec 2007, Galen Seitz wrote:

> Daniel.Roberts at sanofi-aventis.com wrote:
>> Hello All
>>
>> On a redhat system..how can I figure out when rpm was last run?
>> I am trying to figure out if someone besides myself is running RPM...or
>> possibly how if at all a package which I thought got installed has now
>> been removed ed..
>
> This isn't exactly what you want, but it's a start.  This command will
> show all installed packages, sorted by install time.
>
> rpm -qa --last

I'm unsure if you're actually interested in knowing when someone runs 
the rpm binary or not. The Red Hat packaging system can be accessed 
via some shared libraries, so keeping an eye on /bin/rpm won't 
necessarily be an accurate way of knowing when there's been rpm-like 
activity.

It'd probably be more useful to keep an eye on the /var/lib/rpm 
directory or one or more of the database files it contains.

If you have SELinux installed and configured, you can have the audit 
daemon keep an eye on certain files. See /usr/share/doc/audit-* and 
the sample rules files there for information on monitoring a certain 
file or directory.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

On Tue, 2007-12-11 at 14:10 -0800, Nick Aubert wrote:
> Syllable is in fairly early stages of development.  I think of it as
> somewhat equivalent to Linux in the pre-2.0 days.  It probably isn't
> the ideal choice if you just want to get things done.  On the other
> hand, if you manage to get ethernet working under it, you'll probably
> have learned something interesting along the way.  With an OS at this
> stage of development, that's probably the best you can hope for, and
> kind of the whole point.  By the way, Syllable's AFS file system is
> the AtheOS File System, not Andrew File System.
> 
> >From what I've read, ReactOS is basically the same as Wine, but
> without Unix underneath.  So it isn't likely to run Windows programs
> any better than Wine.  I'm not saying this to discourage you from
> trying it out, but you should set your expectations accordingly.  If
> Wine/ReactOS ever does get to the point of drop-in replacement for
> Windows, expect Microsoft to go all out with patent lawsuits on every
> obvious and trivial idea they ever copied from anyone else.
> 
> -Nick

ReactOS is an operating system, albeit a very buggy one.  ReactOS is
being designed to use native Windows 2000 and later hardware drivers.
I don't think this is possible with wine.  I doubt that ReactOS will
get sued successfully barring a change in patent law to cover software,
go to http://www.reactos.org to find out more.  Wine hasn't been sued
where the ReactOS project is employing the same development model.

On Thu, 2007-12-13 at 08:58 -0800, John Jason Jordan wrote:
> On Wed, 12 Dec 2007 23:40:23 -0800
> "drew wymore" <drew.wymore at gmail.com> dijo:
> 
> > > Aha! I did not think of that. Indeed, I do have Comcast. And as far as
> > > I know, they are still playing dirty pool with torrents. After 7.5
> > > hours my average is 22.5 KB/s.
> 
> > Don't go with Qwest (As the ISP). I was visiting my parents over the weekend
> > and until I shutdown my torrents they kept disconnecting me. Maybe go with
> > one of the local places like Hevanet. Call and see if they do any bandwidth
> > throttling or traffic shaping.
> 
> I keep wondering if it is just the settings I have in Ktorrent that are
> the source of the problem, rather than Comcast. For example, all my
> other internet activity is not slower. If they were throttling someone
> using torrents, would that not affect all my traffic?
> 
> I also just noticed in Ktorrent that there is a dropdown for "engine,"
> which lists bitoogle.com, bittorrent.com, bytenova.org,
> isotottents.com, Ktorrents, and mininova.org. It is set to the
> bitoogle.com by default, as I never even knew this dropdown list was
> there. It might have been added during a recent upgrade. I wonder what
> those things do.

They're search engines, for searching for torrents. They have no effect
on your bandwith. Part of the problem is probably that cable modems are
highly asymmetric--back when I followed these things more closely, their
upstream bandwidth was on the order of 128kbps. BitTorrent is designed
to favor users who share more, so your limited upstream bandwidth
hurts. 

Another suggestion, albeit counter-intuitive, is to cap your upstream
bandwidth to 80%. Part of the communications process with TCP requires
sending acknowledgement packets to the sender. If these are getting
dropped or delayed due to congestion, then the sender will re-transmit,
which also hurts your performance.

Finally, you also need to set up port forwarding (assuming you're using
a firewall) for the upstream to work at all, which causes a worse
penalty than having limited upstream bandwidth. Of course, you will also
need to ensure that the port is opened on your host, if you have
firewall rules there also.

There are numerous FAQs out there about BitTorrent which you should
probably read if you're having problem.

Wil



From griffint at pobox.com  Thu Dec 13 09:28:50 2007
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Thu, 13 Dec 2007 09:28:50 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] It worked yesterday...
In-Reply-To: <4761516D.8010801@comcast.net>
References: <4761516D.8010801@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <51701.192.168.254.2.1197566930.squirrel@chinook>

Try resetting or power-cycling the X10 controller. If it has
battery backup you might have to pull the battery for a few seconds.

Also make sure the controller is not overheating. I once set my
old CP-290 controller on top of a modem. The little bit of extra
heat pushed it over the edge. But once it cooled off it's been
fine ever since, and that was seven years ago or more.

Terry

On Thu, 13 Dec 2007, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> I keep wondering if it is just the settings I have in Ktorrent that

or protocol number(s) or even deeper packet inspection. E-mail zips 
along while your torrents crawl.

On Thu, December 13, 2007 9:04 am, Wil Cooley wrote:
> [snip]
>
> What does the 'x10 checksum error' below mean?
>
> [snip]

The fancier X10 controllers have checksums built in to the
serial protocol. The software is saying that things are not
adding up, literally.

This can be caused by several things:
1. The controller itself is misbehaving.
2. Serial communications between the PC and the controller are
   out-of-sync for some reason.
3. The serial port is misconfigured.

Given that it worked recently I'm assuming #1 or #2. Resetting
the controller should clear it up, I hope.

Terry

A firmware update on the modem will also fix this.  If you have a Cisco
firewall/router you may need to do this as well.

The problem may not be filtering.  it may be that the connection table used
by the router is too small.

Also, you may need to use Windows and IE to update the firmware.  The Cisco
update uses an ActiveX control to do most of the work.  It fails
mysteriously with Firefox or any other OS.

On 07 Dec 2007 18:52:37 -0800, Russell Senior <russell at personaltelco.net>
wrote:

> >>>>> "Nick" == Nick Aubert <nickaubert at gmail.com> writes:
>
> Nick> Linux support for Atheros chipsets is pretty good.  Two years
> Nick> ago I had to do quite a bit of work to get the madwifi drivers
> Nick> working on my laptop.  A week ago I set up a Gentoo laptop with
> Nick> an Atheros wifi card, and it was a snap, even with WPA
> Nick> encryption via wpa_supplicant.  I don't know how Knoppix does
> Nick> with madwifi, but kernel support is definitely there.
>
> Madwifi has indeed been one of the more solid linux drivers.  But
> considering that none of them has been *that* solid, it might fall
> into the category of "faint praise".  Historically, the hostap-driver
> for prism chips was really solid.  Some of the other 11b devices had
> decent if divergent support.  I have been using madwifi-old for a
> couple years with the atheros radio in my thinkpad (I am sticking with
> madwifi-old because it works reliably and since I am often diagnosing
> weirdness at PTP nodes, I would rather not have that muddled up by
> having weirdness on my own radio.  I've used madwifi-ng extensively in
> embedded applications, which has been less solid for me.  Madwifi
> (both -old and -ng) relies on a binary blob, the so-called HAL
> (hardware abstraction layer).  Over the last year to 18 months there
> has been a lot of work on the "mac80211" wifi stack for linux, and in
> in the last few months also the ath5k driver for atheros radios.  I
> haven't tried it yet, but my impression from reading the relevant
> mailing lists is that it's still a bit rough.  Which is completely
> understandable, considering the lack of support that most driver
> writers get from hardware vendors.  My guess is that it'll be another
> 6 months before things really start converging on "solid" and wifi
> support gets better on linux.  In the meantime, find whatever life
> raft you can.  "There's hope.  No Luke Skywalker in sight."
>
>  <http://lkml.org/lkml/2006/1/5/671>
>

There has been a big pissing match over binary kernel blobs v.s. binary
firmware blobs.  Some people do not see the difference.  Some claim that
there is a difference.

It is my understanding that the FCC is resisting allowing open sourced
drivers because people would be able to modify the output power of the
radios.  (Not that closed source is a barrier given the right disassembler.)

The biggest problem right now is that there is not one clear interface for
wireless drivers in the kernel.  There is that way the kernel developers do
it, there is the Madwifi people and the hostap interface.  These need to be
combined into one before things will get any better.


From russell at personaltelco.net  Thu Dec 13 18:56:00 2007
From: russell at personaltelco.net (Russell Senior)
Date: 13 Dec 2007 18:56:00 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wifi card
In-Reply-To: <55cf303a0712131348r64eb51ei5030def425366980@mail.gmail.com>
References: <665390.7832.qm@web50612.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
	<55cf303a0712070910o414de0a6hc92eed02274b638c@mail.gmail.com>
	<55ef240d0712071404u3eebe3b6wf04bebac85b160cd@mail.gmail.com>
	<86k5nphp8q.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<55cf303a0712131348r64eb51ei5030def425366980@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <86k5ni3ry7.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Alan" == Alan Olsen <alan.olsen at gmail.com> writes:

Alan> There has been a big pissing match over binary kernel blobs
Alan> v.s. binary firmware blobs.  Some people do not see the
Alan> difference.  Some claim that there is a difference.

There is a difference.  Binary firmware blobs run on the wireless
device and can possibly not work.  Binary kernel blobs run on your CPU
and can panic your box.

Alan> It is my understanding that the FCC is resisting allowing open
Alan> sourced drivers because people would be able to modify the
Alan> output power of the radios.  (Not that closed source is a
Alan> barrier given the right disassembler.)

The FCC rule requires hardware vendors to try to prevent end-users to
exceed mandated limits, which has been interpretted as prohibiting
their (the vendors) release of open source drivers.  Some devices,
software defined radios, are particularly impacted by this, Atheros
radios being an example.  My understanding is that the FCC rule is not
binding on people other than radio hardware vendors creating
open-source drivers.  So, open-source driver hackers are having to
figure a lot of stuff out on their own, which naturally slows things
down.

Alan> The biggest problem right now is that there is not one clear
Alan> interface for wireless drivers in the kernel.  There is that way
Alan> the kernel developers do it, there is the Madwifi people and the
Alan> hostap interface.  These need to be combined into one before
Alan> things will get any better.

There *is* one clear interface direction these days, and that's
mac80211.  Everything else is legacy.  Madwifi folks have said that
their development effort is being directed mostly towards the ath5k
(mac80211 stack) driver these days.  The problem is that mac80211
isn't quite ready for prime time, nor are many of the drivers that use
it.


-- 
Russell Senior, Secretary
russell at personaltelco.net

I have dealt with SQL Ledger just a bit, but it was a while ago.
First, I would suggest uninstall the Synaptic package from your distro, and
install everything from the tar.gz or whatever they use on the SQL Ledger
website.
I have a feeling something in the package is missing, or a requirement, or
some such.  Try from "scratch".  This will be more likely to give you the
installer script, and this will more likely put everything in the right
place.
Apache and PostgresSQL should be able to install those from your distro
packages and use with it.  You also want to be sure you have Perl installed,
and any Perl modules called for by sql-ledger docs, I am guessing
PostgresSQL has a module, maybe some Apache modules, etc.
When I dealt with SQL Ledger it was on RedHat 8 or 9.

Have you tried asking the people at sql-ledger.com for assistance?

From creswick at gmail.com  Fri Dec 14 16:24:58 2007
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Fri, 14 Dec 2007 16:24:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Proper crontab practice, was It worked yesterday...
In-Reply-To: <47631288.5000400@comcast.net>
References: <4761516D.8010801@comcast.net>
	<1197565478.21912.19.camel@willow.odshp.com>
	<36362.192.168.254.2.1197568545.squirrel@chinook>
	<47617B67.5050804@comcast.net> <47617D38.4010502@seitzassoc.com>
	<47631288.5000400@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <c834ec80712141624s6e1d4000g8ef715303b8bd4f5@mail.gmail.com>

On Dec 14, 2007 3:32 PM, Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net> wrote:
>
> It occurs to me that it might be the way I have two shell scripts that
> control X10 modules called at the same time of day. Does cron just
> launch a program based on time of day, and not notice that it just did
> that a microsecond ago?

I'm not certain how cron determines which program to run first if
there are multiple programs scheduled to happen at the same time, but
I would assume it either just runs them sequentially, or forks a
process for each one (probably the later). In any case, I put together
a simple test:

Two scripts (I could have used parameters, but I didn't want to
complicate things with command line args in crontab):

test_a.sh:
-----------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

date +%H:%M:%S:%N > /tmp/a
sleep 5
date +%H:%M:%S:%N >> /tmp/a
------------------------------------

test_b.sh:
-----------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

date +%H:%M:%S:%N > /tmp/b
sleep 5
date +%H:%M:%S:%N >> /tmp/b
------------------------------------

The scripts just write their start and exit times to a file, and sleep
for 5 seconds in between, so there is plenty of opportunity for a
context switch in the middle.

I then set up my crontab as follows:

20 16 * * * /home/rcreswick/tmp/test_a.sh
20 16 * * * /home/rcreswick/tmp/test_b.sh

and I waited for things to go off.  If the apps are run sequentially,
then the first timestamp in /tmp/b will be after the first timestamp
in test_a. If the scripts are run concurrently, then the times will be
interwoven:

$ cat /tmp/a
16:20:01:498972285
16:20:06:503618939

$ cat /tmp/b
16:20:01:507666246
16:20:06:512344760

So, knowing that the commands are running concurrently, then yes, if
they interfere with each other, then we would have to take that into
account through some external locking.

One approach to your problem would be to have a single
manipulate_my_lights.sh script that's run by cron, and then have that
script read a specification of what to do when it is executed.  (Turn
off the house lights, turn off the tree lights, etc..)  Then you would
just have to modify that specification.  This could be as simple as
just a wrapper around the commands you now have in cron:

#!/bin/bash
<first command from crontab>
<second command from crontab>

You could instead estimate how long the first command will take and
space them out, but this would be more reliable, and easier to work
with in the future.

--Rogan

Rogan Creswick wrote:

> I'm not certain how cron determines which program to run first if
> there are multiple programs scheduled to happen at the same time, but
> I would assume it either just runs them sequentially, or forks a
> process for each one (probably the later). In any case, I put together
> a simple test:
<...>
> So, knowing that the commands are running concurrently, then yes, if
> they interfere with each other, then we would have to take that into
> account through some external locking.
> 
> One approach to your problem would be to have a single
> manipulate_my_lights.sh script that's run by cron, and then have that
> script read a specification of what to do when it is executed. ...

That appears to be the way things work. The two scripts I was calling do
indeed have two calls to X10 each, so within a given script, it's not a
problem. The problem exists when there are two scripts that both call
X10. That's when the second one (I presume) hangs waiting for the first
one to finish. Of course, once it's hung, it never sees the other one
finish. I suppose that if I had the time I could learn something about C
programming by studying the code that talks to the serial port and put
in a test to see if some other process is using the port, and if so wait
a short time before trying again. However, the correct solution is, as
you recommend, putting all the calls to X10 in a single script. The
lights operated correctly this morning. Yesterday I separated the two
crontab entries by 10 minutes. It probably would have worked if they
were separated by 1 minute, too. I notice that the CP-290 does take a
few seconds to respond to the command from X10.

Thanks for the analysis.

Regards,

Dick Steffens

Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> I suppose that if I had the time I could learn something about C
> programming by studying the code that talks to the serial port and put
> in a test to see if some other process is using the port, and if so wait
> a short time before trying again. However, the correct solution is, as
> you recommend, putting all the calls to X10 in a single script. 

Alternatively:

*  Include in your script something like:

    while ps ax | grep -q  [x]10
    do
       # wait for other x10 process to complete
       sleep 10
    done

Then you can do X10 stuff without asking yourself "do I have a cron job about
to do something?"


*  have the script read a list of devices to affect

   for light in `cat listoflights`
   do
        x10 _params_ $light
   done

From aaron at bavariati.org  Sat Dec 15 10:24:58 2007
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2007 10:24:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] megaraid_sas write caching?
In-Reply-To: <165DBD80-E5F9-42E9-ABB5-16DFFD9EF1C0@madebyai.com>
References: <165DBD80-E5F9-42E9-ABB5-16DFFD9EF1C0@madebyai.com>
Message-ID: <20071215182458.GI4925@syrinxpc.com>

On Sat, Dec 15, 2007 at 02:34:32AM -0800, Aaron Ten Clay wrote:
> Hey all,
> 
> Just got Gentoo installed on a shiny new Dell PowerEdge 2950 server  
> with an LSI Logic MegaRAID SAS RAID controller. Everything is great  
> except this:
> 
> [   81.028864] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] 1951399936 512-byte hardware sectors  
> (999117 MB)
> [   81.028991] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Write Protect is off
> [   81.029059] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Mode Sense: 1f 00 10 08
> [   81.029121] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Write cache: disabled, read cache:  
> disabled, supports DPO and FUA
> 
> As the kernel reports, both write- and read-caching are disabled. This  
> is grossly obvious during file copies of a few GB or more - the entire  
> system grinds to a halt for 5+ minutes per GB. Even the console is  
> unresponsive.

One usually disables write-caching with RAID.  It makes it much less
likely that you'll end up with an inconsistent RAID volume if there's a
power-cut.  

That said, the little caches on the drives won't help you much, anyway.
Depending on what technique is used for the copying, you're running into
a problem with some implementations of the block caching, readahead
and/or scheduler systems.  Basically, it tries to read as many files
as it can into RAM, then swaps madly, while writing files out, while
it's trying to read more, and trips over its own feet.  I don't know
what kernel config ad optimizations you're using in Gentoo, but poor
choices there could make it worse.

The cp command, I understand, does things in little chunks to prevent
this.

From plug at merlot.com  Sat Dec 15 11:45:59 2007
From: plug at merlot.com (Kurt Sussman)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2007 11:45:59 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Memory leak???
In-Reply-To: <20071214232551.3v2nz05f9cs4ksko@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
References: <20071214232551.3v2nz05f9cs4ksko@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <20071215194559.GU27893@merlot.com>

someone (plug_1 at robinson-west.com) typed this ...
> On a CentOS 4.3 box yum  updated to 4.4 I have been watching the free store
> via top and have been noticing it going down throughout the day.  I've had
> to shut this box off the hard way a couple of times because it was thrashing.
> Question is, what's the culprit?

First, let's change the question.

What is the problem?

Is the load going up? Is daemon response measurably slower? Are
processes dropping core dumps?

> Why isn't the swap space being used?

Because the system hasn't run out of RAM.

Free memory can show as little as 5M. That doesn't mean the system is in
a low-memory state.

> Is there a way to do garbage collection or otherwise get the memory back
> before the system starts to thrash?

Define (and describe) 'thrash'. As Rogan said, if there's no swap usage,
there can be no thrashing.

The linux kernel is better at memory management than you'd think. It won't
reclaim memory until another program needs it, for the most part. "Free"
memory is a bit if a misleading term, you'll want to identify how much your
processes are using, not what 'top' says is free, since the two are pretty
different.
Thrashing could occur for any number of reasons as well, you listed quite a
few services running on that system, as well as mentioned it being a CD
server. Chances are, any 'thrashing' thats occuring is just normal disk
access loading up program data.
Hard drive activity is normal  :)
I've got a couple dev boxes with umpteen gigs of RAM, and still theres
massive disk access to program data, databases, etc.


-- 
Brent Jones
brent at servuhome.net

From ke7ezt at gmail.com  Sat Dec 15 18:42:30 2007
From: ke7ezt at gmail.com (Aaron)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2007 18:42:30 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] The gremlin is back.
In-Reply-To: <47648F1A.7020609@cad2cam.com>
References: <47648F1A.7020609@cad2cam.com>
Message-ID: <376106930712151842x1d7fee63n29072f52d71ceded@mail.gmail.com>

Not sure if this will help but sometimes if there is a CF card or other
flash device in the HP printers your system could be trying to boot from the
flash drive, which will fail.  If you disconnect the printer and reboot it
will not try to boot from the CF card, etc. Although I'm not sure if you
have a similar situation...so this may not help..but just my initial
thoughts.

Good luck!

Aaron

I have not used sqlgrey, nor am I a postgresql expert, so my comments 
are general in nature.
You can use the same server for two different databases serving two 
different sqlgrey implementations.
Since Sqlgrey is written Perl with DBI connectors, there should be a 
config file for sqlgrey to tell it where the server is and the database 
name, or you can just hack the source.

From alan at clueserver.org  Sun Dec 16 17:44:49 2007
From: alan at clueserver.org (Alan)
Date: Sun, 16 Dec 2007 17:44:49 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] ANNOUNCEMENT: PLUG Advanced Topics December 17th 2007
Message-ID: <1197855889.22354.9.camel@kratos.fnordora.org>

[Notice: We will be having a shorter meeting this time. Jax is closing
early for their employee Christmas party.  We will start at 7pm because
of this.]

PLUG Advanced Topics
December 17th, 2007 7pm-8pm 
Jax Bar and Grill 826 SW 2nd Avenue Portland, Oregon

Speaker: John Ronciak <john.ronciak at intel.com>
Topic: Intel and Linux kernel driver development

The LAN Access Division at Intel is responsible for 6 in-kernel upstream
drivers, e100, e1000, ixgb, e1000e, igb, ixgbe and ioatdma.  These
driver require maintenance to keep up with the ever evolving Linux
kernel so we need to keep pushing changes upstream as well.  This work
involves having to blend the Open Source Linux community way of working
with corporate and business mechanisms.  This presentation and
discussion is about how we make that happen as well as how we interact
with the Linux community.

Usual meeting rules apply.




From dmandel at pdxLinux.org  Sun Dec 16 19:57:56 2007
From: dmandel at pdxLinux.org (David Mandel)
Date: Sun, 16 Dec 2007 19:57:56 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Mambo
In-Reply-To: <4765CDBE.9000601@comcast.net>
References: <000001c83f56$22691af0$673b50d0$@net>
	<4765CDBE.9000601@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <eac729460712161957q6068e4c3ua3737a10ddae68f3@mail.gmail.com>

I think the Joomla people would claim that Mambo is a fork of Mambo, and
Joomla is simply a renaming of Mambo.  As I understand, although mambo was
an open source project, the name was owned (as a trademark) by a private
company that was promoting the development of Mambo.  At some point,
there was a disagreement between the Mambo community and the company
that owned the name, which resulted in the two going in separate directions.
The company kept the name and maybe a little bit of the community for their
version.  The rest of the community started developing using the name Joolma.

I don't know how accurate this story is.  It was told to me by a couple
Joolma developers, who were probably somewhat biased.

Joolma is a very popular CMS.  I haven't ever used it, but I have looked
at it and it looks very nice to me.  Joolma uses standard things like
php and mySQL and apache; so it should be fairly easy to setup and
use with most web hosting services.

From ed at alcpress.com  Sun Dec 16 23:46:20 2007
From: ed at alcpress.com (Ed Sawicki)

Subject: [PLUG] Windows symbolic links?

I've had my head down programming for the past several
weeks so I haven't been paying attention. Someone recently
suggested that Windows now has the equivalent of UNIX/Linux
symbolic links in (one of) its filesystems. He didn't have
any details.

to have the functionality of symbolic links. Has anything
else been introduced that has symbolic links functionality?

From bsr at spek.org  Mon Dec 17 07:42:10 2007
From: bsr at spek.org (Brent Rieck)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2007 07:42:10 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Windows symbolic links?
In-Reply-To: <4766294C.2010504@alcpress.com>
References: <4766294C.2010504@alcpress.com>
Message-ID: <476698D2.9080106@spek.org>

Ed Sawicki wrote:
> I've had my head down programming for the past several
> weeks so I haven't been paying attention. Someone recently
> suggested that Windows now has the equivalent of UNIX/Linux
> symbolic links in (one of) its filesystems. He didn't have
> any details.
> 
> I'm aware of NTFS junction points, which I don't consider
> to have the functionality of symbolic links. Has anything
> else been introduced that has symbolic links functionality?

Windows Vista and later has the feature, it appears to be more similar 
to "real" symbolic links than junction points are: "Symbolic links are 
designed to aid in migration and application compatibility with UNIX 
operating systems. Microsoft has implemented its symbolic links to 
function just like UNIX links."

http://msdn2.microsoft.com/en-us/library/aa365680.aspx

wikipedia:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NTFS_symbolic_link

--Brent


From aaron at madebyai.com  Mon Dec 17 10:11:18 2007
From: aaron at madebyai.com (Aaron Ten Clay)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2007 10:11:18 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] megaraid_sas write caching?
In-Reply-To: <20071215182458.GI4925@syrinxpc.com>
References: <165DBD80-E5F9-42E9-ABB5-16DFFD9EF1C0@madebyai.com>
	<20071215182458.GI4925@syrinxpc.com>
Message-ID: <415DB285-6D10-451A-AEBA-66684CF5F6F8@madebyai.com>


On Dec 15, 2007, at 10:24 AM, Aaron Burt wrote:

> On Sat, Dec 15, 2007 at 02:34:32AM -0800, Aaron Ten Clay wrote:
>> Hey all,
>>
>> Just got Gentoo installed on a shiny new Dell PowerEdge 2950 server
>> with an LSI Logic MegaRAID SAS RAID controller. Everything is great
>> except this:
>>
>> [   81.028864] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] 1951399936 512-byte hardware sectors
>> (999117 MB)
>> [   81.028991] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Write Protect is off
>> [   81.029059] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Mode Sense: 1f 00 10 08
>> [   81.029121] sd 0:2:0:0: [sda] Write cache: disabled, read cache:
>> disabled, supports DPO and FUA
>>
>> As the kernel reports, both write- and read-caching are disabled.  
>> This
>> is grossly obvious during file copies of a few GB or more - the  
>> entire
>> system grinds to a halt for 5+ minutes per GB. Even the console is
>> unresponsive.
>
> One usually disables write-caching with RAID.  It makes it much less
> likely that you'll end up with an inconsistent RAID volume if  
> there's a
> power-cut.
>
> That said, the little caches on the drives won't help you much,  
> anyway.
> Depending on what technique is used for the copying, you're running  
> into
> a problem with some implementations of the block caching, readahead
> and/or scheduler systems.  Basically, it tries to read as many files
> as it can into RAM, then swaps madly, while writing files out, while
> it's trying to read more, and trips over its own feet.  I don't know
> what kernel config ad optimizations you're using in Gentoo, but poor
> choices there could make it worse.
>
> The cp command, I understand, does things in little chunks to prevent
> this.
>
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

Thanks for the reply. The server is UPS-backed and the RAID controller  
has it's own battery backup unit. I don't do anything special with the  
kernel, I just like Gentoo's package management. I've tried the copy  
with both cp and rsync, in both cases the servers console becomes  
unusable. I've never seen this before - I have several systems running  
with 3ware raid controllers that respond just fine under heavy disk  
utilization. The kernel also doesn't say write caching is disabled on  
those boxes.

I think what's happening is the kernel isn't buffering writes to the  
RAID controller - irrespective of whether the RAID controller is  
disabling it's own write cache or the caches on each disk.

-Aaron

> >> entire
> >> system grinds to a halt for 5+ minutes per GB. Even the console is
> >> unresponsive.
> >
> > One usually disables write-caching with RAID.  It makes it much less
> > likely that you'll end up with an inconsistent RAID volume if
> > there's a
> > power-cut.
> >
> > That said, the little caches on the drives won't help you much,
> > anyway.
> > Depending on what technique is used for the copying, you're running
> > into
> > a problem with some implementations of the block caching, readahead
> > and/or scheduler systems.  Basically, it tries to read as many files
> > as it can into RAM, then swaps madly, while writing files out, while
> > it's trying to read more, and trips over its own feet.  I don't know
> > what kernel config ad optimizations you're using in Gentoo, but poor
> > choices there could make it worse.
> >
> > The cp command, I understand, does things in little chunks to prevent
> > this.
> >
> > _______________________________________________
> > PLUG mailing list
> > PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> > http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>
> Thanks for the reply. The server is UPS-backed and the RAID controller
> has it's own battery backup unit. I don't do anything special with the
> kernel, I just like Gentoo's package management. I've tried the copy
> with both cp and rsync, in both cases the servers console becomes
> unusable. I've never seen this before - I have several systems running
> with 3ware raid controllers that respond just fine under heavy disk
> utilization. The kernel also doesn't say write caching is disabled on
> those boxes.
>
> I think what's happening is the kernel isn't buffering writes to the
> RAID controller - irrespective of whether the RAID controller is
> disabling it's own write cache or the caches on each disk.
>
> -Aaron
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>

Install the LSI Linux raid management software, and you can then view/set
the options your kernel is using.
http://www.lsi.com/support/downloads/


-- 
Brent Jones
brent at servuhome.net

From jeme at brelin.net  Mon Dec 17 14:57:00 2007
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2007 16:57:00 -0600 (CST)
Subject: [PLUG] Low cost fileserver
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0712171656220.4108@shadow>

Hi!

So I'm looking for some kind of low cost, low power fileserver.  I think 
either it should be in the $200 range and support two IDE drives (yeah, 
that's the power problem, isn't it?) or should be under $100 and support 
USB 2.0 (for external drive enclosures).

Right now, it looks like the very best bet is the Linksys NSLU2 NAS 
device. Since it runs Linux, the source has been released and, from that, 
other distributions have been reverse-engineered onto the platform.  See:

<URL: http://www.nslu2-linux.org/wiki/Main/HomePage >

This device is about $80.

This would require, however, a good external drive enclosure.  I imagine 
something that holds 4 disks would be ideal.  These can be found for about 
$130 without rails for 3.5" hard disks.  So let's call it $150.

So I'm seeing a low power linux box for $230 that supports four hard 
disks.

Can anyone suggest something that would beat that?

I think all I really need is SAMBA and FTP, but the full Debian 
capabability of the NSLU2 makes me think I could run a torrent client, 
Household Wiki, or something else mildly useful.

J.

From krisa at subtend.net  Mon Dec 17 18:12:24 2007
From: krisa at subtend.net (Kris)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2007 18:12:24 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] vlan
Message-ID: <47672C88.3040809@subtend.net>

For those curious how to use VLANs in Debian, here is a config I have in
production:

/etc/network/interfaces:

auto eth1
iface eth1 inet static
    address 172.1.1.101
    netmask 255.255.255.0

auto eth1.16
iface eth1.16 inet static
    address 10.16.1.1
    netmask 255.255.0.0
    pre-up /sbin/ifconfig eth1 up
    pre-up /sbin/vconfig add eth1 16

auto eth1.18
iface eth1.18 inet static
    address 10.18.1.1
    netmask 255.255.0.0
    pre-up /sbin/ifconfig eth1 up
    pre-up /sbin/vconfig add eth1 18


-- 
I'm just a packet pusher.

>There's a tipping point for both, naturally.
>
>I won't go for a full PC option for power concerns (though for price,
>surely that's the way to go).

Have you checked the current draw of a new, good, mid-power atx supply 
vs the collection of wall-warts that will be involved in powering the 
external usb enclosure(s)?

With a slower cpu, but a new (micro atx?) motherboard, your drives are 
probably going to consume more power than the PC.  Putting everything 
on one large power supply is likely to be more efficient -- it may 
hardly notice the presence of cpu+mobo in comparison to the drives.

So, get a random PIII computer from Free Geek, then buy the most 
efficient, cool-running drives and power-supply you can afford?

--Eric

    http://scratchcomputing.com

From russell at personaltelco.net  Mon Dec 17 22:21:29 2007
From: russell at personaltelco.net (Russell Senior)
Date: 17 Dec 2007 22:21:29 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] FCC ID lookup
Message-ID: <86ejdkv7yu.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>


Alan was asking about a wireless access point at Paddy's this evening
after the advanced topics talk.  Turns out it was a Netgear WNR834M, a
sexy looking device except that it doesn't have visible antennas.
Wanting to know more about it, I thought I'd show him the FCC (like
GCC but completely different) website where you can find out stuff
about radiating devices using the FCC ID as a lookup key.

The website is here: 

  <https://fjallfoss.fcc.gov/oetcf/eas/reports/GenericSearch.cfm>

All wireless cards and access points (and lots of other stuff too)
will be labelled on the outside with an FCC ID.  In the case of
Paddy's gear, it was: PY306100038

On the generic search form, you type the first three characters into
the 'Grantee Code' field, and the remaining characters into the
'Product Code' field and the click the 'Start Search' button.  That
will return one or more hits.  In our case, we get one.  Click on
"Detail" in the "Display Exhibits" column, which will result in a list
(for this device) of 12 exhibits, pdf files containing information
filed by the applicant.  Typically, the most interesting will be
"Internal Photos" and "Test Report", but any of the exhibits could
yield interesting information.

For another example, to see the insides of the MetroFi gear, take a
peak at FCC-ID: RV7-DBE1010.


-- 
Russell Senior, Secretary
russell at personaltelco.net

C:\Users\m0gely>mklink
Creates a symbolic link.

MKLINK [[/D] | [/H] | [/J]] Link Target

         /D      Creates a directory symbolic link.  Default is a file
                 symbolic link.
         /H      Creates a hard link instead of a symbolic link.
         /J      Creates a Directory Junction.
         Link    specifies the new symbolic link name.
         Target  specifies the path (relative or absolute) that the new
                 link refers to.

C:\Users\m0gely>

From plug_1 at robinson-west.com  Wed Dec 19 18:39:36 2007
From: plug_1 at robinson-west.com (someone)

Subject: [PLUG] Computer Science ap PSU a nightmare
Message-ID: <20071219183936.qkx491rrc0gssg0w@xerxes.robinson-west.com>

Anyone else find PSU's computer science program next to impossible to get
through?  If the physics and Calculus don't stop ya, it seems that Karla
Fant will.  Programming Systems is called an intro course, but there's
nothing intro about it.

I've run into difficulties with the academic policy.  Specifically,
the academic warning policy.  PSU is in the dark ages when it comes
to students dropping courses on time.  You go on warning if you
cut your credit load in half.  PCC, last I checked, doesn't worry
about credit load.  I dropped programming systems this fall, one
of 2 courses I was signed up for.  I dropped it before it even
started because the online format wasn't going to make the vague
assignments any easier.  Write a pseudo real estate program is
pretty out there for instructions.  Asking students to do this
on their own in 2 weeks time seems downright absurd to me.

The advice from the IT world, I have a friend there, is to get a
different degree and forget about computer science because I won't
learn what I need to know anyways.  With 28 PSU credits so far and
a few withdrawals, I'm worried about how long it will take to get
off of warning regardless of how I do in future coursework.  My
overall gpa is above a 2.0, but I guess that's being ignored.  I
can't help but wonder if missing grade had anything to do with that.
